  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4c4566c7-a8c5-4c59-8b45-73af3a4a7385'

  <span id="freeText11304396538231875792" style="display:none">Strange things are afoot at Fablehaven. Someone or something has released a plague that transforms beings of light into creatures of darkness. Seth discovers the problem in its infancy, but as the infectious disease spreads, it becomes clear that the preserve cannot hold out for long.<br /><br />In dire need of help, the Sorensons question where to turn. The Sphinx has always given sound advice–but is he a traitor? Inside the Quiet Box, Vanessa might have information that could lead to a cure–but can she be trust?<br /><br />Meanwhile, Kendra and members of the Knights of the Dawn must journey to a distant preserve and retrieve another hidden artifact. Will the Society of the Evening Star recover it first? Will the plague eclipse all light at Fablehaven? Find out in Fablehaven: Grip of the Shadow Plague.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer357904525370593277">Grip of the Shadow Plague (Fablehaven, #3), Brandon Mull<br/><br/>Fablehaven: Grip of the Shadow Plague is the third novel in the Fablehaven fantasy series written by Brandon Mull. The book was released on April 21, 2008. <br/><br/>This book picks up where "Fablehaven: Rise of the Evening Star" leaves off, during the same summer of the second year at Fablehaven. Sometime throughout the Summer, Kendra is requested by the Captain of 'The Knights Of Dawn' that she should be recruited, and for the first time, Kendra an</span>
  <span id="freeText357904525370593277" style="display:none">Grip of the Shadow Plague (Fablehaven, #3), Brandon Mull<br /><br />Fablehaven: Grip of the Shadow Plague is the third novel in the Fablehaven fantasy series written by Brandon Mull. The book was released on April 21, 2008. <br /><br />This book picks up where "Fablehaven: Rise of the Evening Star" leaves off, during the same summer of the second year at Fablehaven. Sometime throughout the Summer, Kendra is requested by the Captain of 'The Knights Of Dawn' that she should be recruited, and for the first time, Kendra and Warren must visit another magical preserve, called Lost Mesa, that is located in the central state of Arizona. <br /><br />They resign there, with Lieutenant Dougan Fisk, and dragon tamer Gavin Rose (whom Kendra has feelings for). Another hidden artifact must be recovered from Lost Mesa, before The Society unveils it first. However, Patton Burgess had already recovered the artifact and taken it to Fablehaven. Meanwhile, Seth discovers that someone, or something, has released a plague throughout Fablehaven, before the others but as the disease spreads throughout the preserve, it is clear that they can no longer protect the preserve. <br /><br />Creatures of light are transformed into creatures of dark. As light creatures can enter most places throughout the preserve, the same rules apply to the more darkened form of them. Seth is stuck at Fablehaven, where he, his grandparents, Tanu, and Coulter must try to solve the mystery of a new plague that is transforming the magical creatures. <br /><br />Seth discovers that he has gained new abilities with destroying Fablehaven's revenant. He is able to shadow-walk, hear the voices of prisoners from the dungeon that dwell underneath the main house, and speak the language of many creatures such as imps, goblins, trolls, demons, and giants. (Kendra can recharge magical artifacts, see in the dark, control fairies, glow very brightly, and talk to many magical creatures like Seth.) After coming back Kendra learns that Warren, Grandpa, Grandma, Dale, Tanu ,and Coulter are shadows. <br /><br />However, she also learns that Seth has brought Patton to the future for three days using the Chronometer. Patton helps Seth and Kendra shut down the plague using a stone provided by the Fairy Queen and Lena dies when they shut down the plague. After the plague is stopped Dougan came to escort Kendra home. He also said the Sphinx was their greatest enemy.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیستم ماه ژانویه سال 2012 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: پنجگانه افسانه کتاب سوم شیوع طاعون سایه؛ نویسنده: براندن (براندون) مال (مول)؛ مترجم میلاد فشتمی؛ تهران، بهنام، 1390، در 500ص؛ از مجموعه پنجگانه افسانه - کتاب سوم؛ شابک 9789645668714؛ موضوع داستانهای کودکان از نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 21م<br /><br />شیوع طاعون سایه: داستان نبرد تاریخی نور و تاریکی است؛ «براندون مول» در سومین کتاب از پنجگانه «افسانه» همانند دو جلد پیشین، ضمن روایت داستانی جذاب و زیبا، تلاش کرده تا مفاهیمی ارزشمند را به خوانشگر خود منتقل کند، و امیدوار است این مفاهیم هرچه بیشتر در نسل جوان امروز شکل بگیرد و پرورش یابد؛ از جمله این مفاهیم می‌توان به «فداکاری»، «ریسک‌ پذیری منطقی«، و «درست اندیشیدن، در لحظات بحرانی» اشاره کرد، که «کندرا»، و «ست» (دو شخصیت اصلی داستان)، در خلال ماجراهای کتاب، آنها را یاد می‌گیرند، و بیش از پیش با توانایی‌های خویش آشنا می‌شوند و هرچه بیشتر خود را باور می‌کنند؛<br /><br />نقل از متن: آشیانه‌ افسانه بار دیگر در خطر است: نیرویی نامریی نور موجودات جادویی پناهگاه را می‌بلعد و آنها را به موجوداتی خبیث و تاریک تبدیل می‌کند؛ ست خیلی زود از این موضوع مطلع می‌شود، ولی طاعون سایه به سرعت در حال گسترش است. فرصت کمی تا سقوط پناهگاه باقی مانده و سورنسون‌ها به کمک نیاز دارند، اما به چه کسی می‌توانند اعتماد کنند؟...»؛ پایان نقل ا. شربیانی</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2214677967" />
    <a title="George Jankovic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48492241-george-jankovic"><img alt="George Jankovic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492530766p2/48492241.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2214677967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13884837139796841121">Brandon Mull developed the world of this awesome series so much more in this book. I really love how the species were described, each with different characters traits. The centaurs are proud and conceited. The fairies crave attention, always check their looks and like to gossip. The satyrs are playful and love girls (dryads). The naiads disdain all the land-based creatures, but their favorite pastime is drowning humans. Etc etc. <br/><br/>One great thing in this book is how much more we got into character</span>
  <span id="freeText13884837139796841121" style="display:none">Brandon Mull developed the world of this awesome series so much more in this book. I really love how the species were described, each with different characters traits. The centaurs are proud and conceited. The fairies crave attention, always check their looks and like to gossip. The satyrs are playful and love girls (dryads). The naiads disdain all the land-based creatures, but their favorite pastime is drowning humans. Etc etc. <br /><br />One great thing in this book is how much more we got into character thoughts and feelings since they were often separated. Kendra is wonderful as always. And I really liked Seth in this book. He is still naughty but tries to not be as careless while staying brave. Gavin is a great new character.<br /><br />5 stars. Enjoy!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13884837139796841121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436096659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12146561639018927235"><i>How is it even possible for this storyline to get better with each new book, ( but yet it does )</i><br/><br/><b>Simply Brilliant....Book 4, Here I Come!!!</b></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_145559452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145559452" />
    <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent"><img alt="Aaron Vincent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360133074p2/2924544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145559452?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Vincent" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent">Aaron Vincent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=ya-mg-fantasy">ya-mg-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145559452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8867398790245641549"><b>Originally Posted on <a href='http://guygonegeek.wordpress.com/2011/03/05/review-grip-of-the-shadow-plaguefablehaven-3-by-brandon-mull/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guy Gone Geek</a></b><br/><br/>The middle part of fantasy series are always the trickiest. The world is already established in the first book(s) and information about the series-long plot are held back for the finale. Middle part books are always the one that is the most forgettable and there are cases when these books are just fodders. Such is the case in Michael Scott’s Secrets of the Immortal Nicholas Flamel and even Rick Riordan’s Percy Jackson. I love both of these series but if you ask </span>
  <span id="freeText8867398790245641549" style="display:none"><b>Originally Posted on <a href="http://guygonegeek.wordpress.com/2011/03/05/review-grip-of-the-shadow-plaguefablehaven-3-by-brandon-mull/" rel="nofollow noopener">Guy Gone Geek</a></b><br /><br />The middle part of fantasy series are always the trickiest. The world is already established in the first book(s) and information about the series-long plot are held back for the finale. Middle part books are always the one that is the most forgettable and there are cases when these books are just fodders. Such is the case in Michael Scott’s Secrets of the Immortal Nicholas Flamel and even Rick Riordan’s Percy Jackson. I love both of these series but if you ask me what happened in The Necromancer or Battle of the Labyrinth, I will likely just give you a two-sentence long summary or worse, a blank stare. But if you ask me about the first book or the finale, I would tell you everything in detail and with vigor your ears might bleed.<br /><br />It is one of the most common writing traps. Authors tends to play some of their aces in the first book to hook you in and the rest of their remaining aces in the finale to blow your mind and make a lasting impression. Now, it’s either Brandon Mull is a cheater or a magician that he has endless supply of aces or he is just skillful on distributing fair amounts of it in his books. I personally prefer the former for it is way more wicked.<br /><br />Grip of the Shadow Plague starts several weeks after the events of Rise of the Evening Star with Kendra being invited to join the Knights of Dawn, a secret society which function is to protect all the magical preserves across the globe. Right after joining the society, she was assigned to retrieve another secret artifact hidden at a preserve in Arizona, The Lost Mesa. Meanwhile at Fablehaven, Seth is not missing out any actions as the creatures – even those without fallen states – are turning into creatures of darkness. Creatures known to be gentle and nurturing are transformed into wild and savage beasts. The Shadow Plague is spreading fast and they must find a way to stop it before in consumes the entire magical preserve making Fablehaven just a part of history.<br /><br />Brandon Mull continues to impress me by writing the third book in this ever-imaginative series in dual narratives. The transitions were not seamless but both were engaging and very exciting. The Lost Mesa is a very interesting preserve. Creatures that inhabits this preserve are different from Fablehaven(there are zombies!), albeit much more dangerous. It also follows an entirely different set of rules and hides its own secrets. Fablehaven itself has its own deep dark secrets and a grim history that were exposed in this book. This is what makes this series truly, well, magical – the preserves are characters of its own.<br /><br />Grip of the Shadow Plague, literally and figuratively, took a much darker turn compared to its predecessors. There were lives sacrificed, and the characters’ motives lies within the thin line that separates good and evil. There was also a time travel subplot that ended with a tragic and heartbreaking conclusion. Our heroes were more matured – Kendra has less doubt in herself than before and there were lesser amount of times I wanted to scream at Seth – but nothing prepared them for the dire events happened in this book. The only flaw I can complain about in this installment is how Mull kept his characters clueless about a certain conflict even if the answer was staring at their faces, or Kendra’s face at least. This isn’t enough to topple one star, though, cause this particular conflict is not really the focus of this book and there were too much going on for me to be distracted and forget about it at the most crucial points of the story. I think its part of Kendra’s characterization, anyway. She’s too trusting to suspect anyone. These things I’m sure will happen in the next book, Secrets of the Dragon Sanctuary: enemies will be unmasked, hearts will be broken, Brandon Mull will continue to show off his storytelling prowess and Aaron, once again, will be left breathless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8867398790245641549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_32897975" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32897975" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/369741-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219718301p2/369741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32897975?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/369741-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32897975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7904166548366024282">I enjoy the Fablehaven series, and this third one was very good. I like Mull's creativity and energy. I appreciate his ongoing discussion of the nature of good and evil, the power of our choices, and in this one, the consequences of choosing to believe or not. I liked the way this book expanded the characters and locations of the story. And Patton Burgess is awesome! :) <br/><br/>I read this book first alone, but then I reread it aloud with my husband. In reading aloud, we discovered an annoying flaw. Mul</span>
  <span id="freeText7904166548366024282" style="display:none">I enjoy the Fablehaven series, and this third one was very good. I like Mull's creativity and energy. I appreciate his ongoing discussion of the nature of good and evil, the power of our choices, and in this one, the consequences of choosing to believe or not. I liked the way this book expanded the characters and locations of the story. And Patton Burgess is awesome! :) <br /><br />I read this book first alone, but then I reread it aloud with my husband. In reading aloud, we discovered an annoying flaw. Mull does well with action scenes, but whenever he is summarizing the past storyline or when he is bridging to a new scene, his writing becomes painfully stilted and boring. I skimmed over these parts when reading silently to myself, but reading them aloud is awful! Some prime examples are at the beginning when Kendra is sitting alone in the dungeon and worse, the chapter in the Atlanta airport. Mull's editor should pay better attention and help him refine his writing skills!<br /><br />However, the story is still fun, creative, exciting fantasy, so I recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7904166548366024282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2991969216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2991969216" />
    <a title="Henry Lin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101537778-henry-lin"><img alt="Henry Lin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2991969216?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Lin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Lin" href="/user/show/101537778-henry-lin">Henry Lin</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2991969216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14000927859544448963">Very interesting theme. It has the traditional good vs. evil but adds twists to it. This theme was particularly apparent in the first two books and is even explicitly stated by Grandpa Sorenson: The creatures of Fablehaven are neither good nor evil. They are only categorized into lightness and darkness. For example, Naiads drown people when they come near, but they are creatures of light. <br/>In this book, there's a new variable: the shadow plague. This plague turns creatures of light into creatures</span>
  <span id="freeText14000927859544448963" style="display:none">Very interesting theme. It has the traditional good vs. evil but adds twists to it. This theme was particularly apparent in the first two books and is even explicitly stated by Grandpa Sorenson: The creatures of Fablehaven are neither good nor evil. They are only categorized into lightness and darkness. For example, Naiads drown people when they come near, but they are creatures of light. <br />In this book, there's a new variable: the shadow plague. This plague turns creatures of light into creatures of darkness. This furthers the evidence of goodness vs. evil with twists. Light creatures turning dark means that there is no goodness/evil for the magical creatures. For a magical creature, good/evil does not exist. Honestly, this is probably one of the most interesting themes I've seen. It was mentioned that the Sphinx could possibly be evil in the second book. For the purposes of spoilers, I won't tell you whether he is evil or not, but if he is, he probably believes what he is doing is right, so that could be very interesting for the theme. The character development from book 2 to this book is a little too fast, from Seth and Kendra kind of hating each other to hugs and kisses for everyone. Still not completely sure as to how I think of this series yet, but it’s certainly growing on me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14000927859544448963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23236121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23236121" />
    <a title="John Conrad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/784106-john-conrad"><img alt="John Conrad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200981879p2/784106.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23236121?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Conrad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Conrad" href="/user/show/784106-john-conrad">John Conrad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/784106-john-conrad?shelf=books-for-young-people">books-for-young-people</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer23236121&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23236121" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3814177419231761403">This was a really well-written sequel that answered most of the questions from the last two. I enjoyed seeing Seth grow up a little bit, and Kendra's new relationship should be interesting for the future. I thought that death was treated pretty casually, especially the first one. I had to read back and confirm that the character had really died because it happened so quickly and without much comment. My favorite sequence has to be the Haunted Mesa with all its twists and turns, but is wrapped up</span>
  <span id="freeText3814177419231761403" style="display:none">This was a really well-written sequel that answered most of the questions from the last two. I enjoyed seeing Seth grow up a little bit, and Kendra's new relationship should be interesting for the future. I thought that death was treated pretty casually, especially the first one. I had to read back and confirm that the character had really died because it happened so quickly and without much comment. My favorite sequence has to be the Haunted Mesa with all its twists and turns, but is wrapped up quite neatly at the end as well. I had reserved judgement on the Sphynx thinking there might have been some cool excuse for his behavior, but was a little disappointed to find the truth confirmed. I hope we get more of an explanation in the next book as to why he chose the path he did. Is he just a flat "bad guy" or is there some combination of good and bad, or reasons he chose the bad side. <br /><br />Overall this was a very good read, and enjoyable from start to finish. If I seem to be picking out flaws, it's because I'm actually trying to be a more critical reader. After all, if every book gets five stars, where's the room for improvement? I want goodreads to put in half stars so I can be more precise in my ratings. This was a good solid 4 stars, however, and, in my opinion good for readers at many levels. It might be above the heads of a few beginners, but it should be okay for ages 10 and up, though they might struggle a little with the vocabulary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3814177419231761403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Audrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5630113-audrey"><img alt="Audrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572483937p2/5630113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

As the third book in the series, it is definitely necessary to read them in order. <br /><br />It’s a pretty long book for MG, but a lot happens, so it never drags. And I only wanted to strangle Seth about half the time instead of all the time. He’s starting to learn. There are also quite a few magical creatures seen, which made me a bit nostalgic for Narnia.<br /><br /><a href="https://audreytheeditor.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Book Blog</a></span>

<div id="review_1894025759" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894025759" />
    <a title="Mary ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37766180-mary"><img alt="Mary ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555156334p2/37766180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894025759?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ♥" href="/user/show/37766180-mary">Mary ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37766180-mary?shelf=faves">faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894025759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1798619988223712492">5/5 stars<br/><br/><b> When your only option is to jump, you jump and try to make it work. </b><br/><br/>This felt like such a huge journey, even if the book was not that big, something that makes me super excited for the rest of the books. The reason for this is because through the pages of Grip of the Shadow Plague, I met a lot of new characters and creatures, learned more information about the old ones and dove deeper into the world of Fablehaven. Things like the Knights of Dawn and Patton Burgess got explained, and I </span>
  <span id="freeText1798619988223712492" style="display:none">5/5 stars<br><br><b> When your only option is to jump, you jump and try to make it work. </b><br><br>This felt like such a huge journey, even if the book was not that big, something that makes me super excited for the rest of the books. The reason for this is because through the pages of Grip of the Shadow Plague, I met a lot of new characters and creatures, learned more information about the old ones and dove deeper into the world of Fablehaven. Things like the Knights of Dawn and Patton Burgess got explained, and I filled my head with tons of new content.<br><br>Not only that, but this book also has a dual POV at some point, as the siblings Sorenson get separated for two different adventures, something that excited me even more. Brandon Mull's imagination was very vivid and a lot of the things that happened set a complex path for the rest of the books. We also got to see more of Tanu and Warren (although I wanted to see more of Coulter too, since he seems like a very interesting character).<br><br>Kendra's adventure was wild and full of magic and difficult situations, as she journeyed to find artifacts before the Evening Star and its leader. It made me forget how old Kendra truly is at some point, as she acted in a very mature, adult-like way.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532260054ra/26012190.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Seth's adventure was far more mystical and weird and unique, and I felt myself worrying more about him than Kendra, although both parts of the story excited me. At some point, they collided together, and things turned so, so wild since then.<br><br>The plot was quick, full of close-to-death situations, mystery and twists, and I absolutely adored every single part of it, even if it felt like a never ending journey because of the information. The conspiracy that was revealed in the end of book 2 brought an even bigger amount of peril, and the siblings handled it in a very clever and careful way, considering how serious the situation was. I also was happy to see that this time, Kendra and Seth didn't have their grandparents to help them but had to rely on themselves to save Fablehaven, something that made me extremely happy, as their physical and mental growth appeared.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Patton and Lena though! This twist was my absolute favorite, as they were truly an adorable couple, that still had to go through difficult situations, something that proves that when it comes to relationships, things are never easy, and it really warmed my heart on how the overcame everything with love and faith to each other. It all seemed like a very important representation of a relationship in a middle grade novel.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, this book dealt with some very serious matters, such as life and death, the meaning of sacrifice, light and dark, dealing with trauma and so many other things, the portrayal of which is important in books for younger readers. It never fails to surprise me how middle grade books deal with so heavy topics in a way that brings hope, without shying away from the darker nature of the matters.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532260054ra/26012191.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It just made me happy to come back in this world again, and I am really excited to see how the story proceeds in the last two books ♥<br><br>Be strong, everyone, and never stop believing in yourselves ♥ There is light even in the darkest of days, and you can always find your way ♥ Until the next review, keep reading :D<br><br>~Mary♥</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1798619988223712492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1574732627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1574732627" />
    <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss"><img alt="C.P. Cabaniss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468698183p2/9656259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1574732627?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.P. Cabaniss" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss">C.P. Cabaniss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=yallfest">yallfest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574732627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6067849326679275067">I have fallen in love with this series. When I first read <i>Fablehaven</i> two years ago, I remember liking but not loving it. Both <i>The Rise of the Evening Star</i> and <i>Grip of the Shadow Plague</i> have jumped more into the love category. <br/><br/>The characters are excellent. Both Kendra and Seth have developed a lot over the course of the series and it is nice to see this development. Their relationship is realistic, showing the positive and negative sides of having a sibling. <br/><br/>This installment takes us to new locat</span>
  <span id="freeText6067849326679275067" style="display:none">I have fallen in love with this series. When I first read <i>Fablehaven</i> two years ago, I remember liking but not loving it. Both <i>The Rise of the Evening Star</i> and <i>Grip of the Shadow Plague</i> have jumped more into the love category. <br /><br />The characters are excellent. Both Kendra and Seth have developed a lot over the course of the series and it is nice to see this development. Their relationship is realistic, showing the positive and negative sides of having a sibling. <br /><br />This installment takes us to new locations as some of our characters leave Fablehaven to go on a mission to find another artifact. We have dragons, time travel, darkness overtaking light, and still our characters manage to maintain hope. <br /><br />I'm very excited to continue onto the next book in the series and hope that it continues this upward trend. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6067849326679275067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24390947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24390947" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/984874-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1206673369p2/984874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24390947?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/984874-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young adult and up</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/984874-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/984874-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24390947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8789385495304433417">Seth is growing up and making better decisions. Brandon has fallen into a writer's trap of alternating story lines between two primary characters. And finally, the series became so-so.<br/><br/>All that said, Grip of the Shadow Plague was another good read from the Fablehaven series for young adult readers and should keep their interest. Both my wife and I agree that this will start to appeal more to boys with Seth's new-found "wisdom" (and I use quotes because he isn't there yet, but well on his way).<br/><br/>If </span>
  <span id="freeText8789385495304433417" style="display:none">Seth is growing up and making better decisions. Brandon has fallen into a writer's trap of alternating story lines between two primary characters. And finally, the series became so-so.<br /><br />All that said, Grip of the Shadow Plague was another good read from the Fablehaven series for young adult readers and should keep their interest. Both my wife and I agree that this will start to appeal more to boys with Seth's new-found "wisdom" (and I use quotes because he isn't there yet, but well on his way).<br /><br />If I remember correctly, the first two Fablehaven books seemed to each tell their own story, all by themselves. This one, the writer came to the forefront with a technique that felt "forced." With Kendra off on assignment (yeah, that's right, but I won't tell you why or where), Seth was left back at Fablehaven with a lot of problems facing that stronghold of magic. As a result, the story alternates by chapter through a fair amount of the book between Kendra's problems and Seth's. Rather than let time and nature guide the story, giving the book a life of its own, I felt the author was pushed into a writing regimen that didn't work particularly well. Whenever this happens in a novel, the story loses its focus and that's what happened here.<br /><br />The story became somewhat bland and any tension-building was lost each time the scene changed from one location to another. I've put down books because of this and I hope that it doesn't happen to the fourth of the series.<br /><br />Finally, Kendra is developing powers that are not only making her a target for the bad guys, but also powers that are protecting her against those same bad guys. It puts the author into a precarious position, having to come up with something that will truly challenge our young heroine.<br /><br />Seth rides to the rescue. While Kendra gets to go off for some truly disgusting stuff, which would thrill Seth, he languishes back at boring old Fablehaven. Never mind that creatures of light are turning into creatures of darkness and infecting the rest of the group. Never mind that Seth grows serious when left to his own designs and starts to realize that one really must give thought before action. Never mind that he even has to hide what he's doing because if Kendra ever found out, he'd never live it down. All of this brings to Seth a new-found maturity that leaves us pleased with his progress and smiling at the end.<br /><br />Only the loss of tension through scene-switching (which didn't work well in this case) drug this down into the four-star realm. Brandon's writing stumbled only a couple of times (rare for him), but nothing grammatically horrible--just enough for me to notice and puzzle for a moment.<br /><br />One particularly astute observation struck me on this book and it is worth mentioning. "Total unbelief is a powerful inhibitor."<br /><br />And with that, I leave you my thoughts and review of Grip of the Shadow Plague.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8789385495304433417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1770876772" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1770876772" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770876772?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/32312578-grip-of-the-shadow-plague">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770876772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2349088040314472103"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>When you have a state-wide blackout, there isn’t much more you can do than grab a book… and why not make it an old favourite that is in desperate need of a reread? Well, that’s what I decide to do last night anyway and I’m so glad I did. This series just gives me life. God, it’s honestly the most well-written middle grade series I have ever laid my hands on! If you were iffy about the first book in the series, I can promise that it gets better and better with each book. The characters a</span>
  <span id="freeText2349088040314472103" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />When you have a state-wide blackout, there isn’t much more you can do than grab a book… and why not make it an old favourite that is in desperate need of a reread? Well, that’s what I decide to do last night anyway and I’m so glad I did. This series just gives me life. God, it’s honestly the most well-written middle grade series I have ever laid my hands on! If you were iffy about the first book in the series, I can promise that it gets better and better with each book. The characters are just so well-developed. Kendra and Seth both make fantastic protagonists, probably because they’re so relatable and realistic. I also adore Warren and the entire Fablehaven gang. We get a couple of new characters in this sequel too and I completely fell head of heels for one of them in particular…<br /><br />I also adore how this series isn’t afraid to get dark and gritty, despite the age of the target audience. Mull never pulls his punches and I adore that he treats his MG audience to more mature content than other series. This books manages to throw plot twist after plot twist to keep you on your toes. By now, I don’t think you can trust any character fully. You’re always waiting for some sort of betrayal or something unexpected to happen! I also love how we got to explore the lore/mythology on a larger scale in this book. We discover new creatures, new preserves, new artifacts - just a lot of fresh, new exciting stuff that ups the stakes.<br /><br /><b>Overall?</b><br /><br />This series is beautiful. It’s so well-written and cleverly constructed. I honestly recommend it to all MG fans and it’s one of those series that I just want to force on everyone and anyone that will let me. I definitely plan on finishing a reread of this series by the end of the year. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2349088040314472103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_22180019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22180019" />
    <a title="Garrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/802571-garrett"><img alt="Garrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1211829844p2/802571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22180019?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Garrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Garrett" href="/user/show/802571-garrett">Garrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22180019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17977592102921262339">I think I like this book the best so far out of the series. It felt more complete and whole somehow. I assume it is at least partly because Brandon is becoming a better writer. But I think it also has to do with an improved plot structure and more intense, realistic conflict.<br/><br/>Setting: Still mostly at Fablehaven, but with explorations of even more of the area. Also, Kendra does get to go to a meeting of a secret society (held in a house like a castle) and then to another preserve in Arizona. So, f</span>
  <span id="freeText17977592102921262339" style="display:none">I think I like this book the best so far out of the series. It felt more complete and whole somehow. I assume it is at least partly because Brandon is becoming a better writer. But I think it also has to do with an improved plot structure and more intense, realistic conflict.<br /><br />Setting: Still mostly at Fablehaven, but with explorations of even more of the area. Also, Kendra does get to go to a meeting of a secret society (held in a house like a castle) and then to another preserve in Arizona. So, fun stuff.<br /><br />Plot: Again, I felt like Brandon has gotten better at plotting. I read through the book fairly quickly, and never felt like there was a lag in the story.<br /><br />Conflict: Lots of great conflict with the shadow plague happening, the dealing with Vanessa, the artifact at Lost Mesa, the society meeting, the suspicions about the Sphinx, and Seth's conflict with obedience. The introduction of the former Fablehaven keeper felt a bit deus ex machina and made the resolution seem a bit easy, but I still enjoyed how it brought things full circle that were introduced in the first book.<br /><br />Character: A couple new main characters, including a love interest for Kendra kept things moving. I also like how Brandon shows the growth of Seth (that kid's actions sometimes make me want to scream - and then I realize that he is imaginary even though he acts like a lot of boys I know and have known).<br /><br />Text: Nothing unbelievably special here. I don't remember thinking that the text got in the way of the story or pulled me out of the story, so I suppose that means he did a great job!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17977592102921262339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5103038665228185221">This is a book I will like more in the future as I think back on it than I do right now having just finished it. The storyline was fine, but the execution of it fell flat for me. I was never completely drawn into the story until about the last hundred pages. Most of this was due to the splitting of the storyline with Kendra on a mission at Lost Mesa in Arizona while Seth stayed at Fablehaven and had adventures there. It felt very choppy as we jumped back and forth between the two storylines. May</span>
  <span id="freeText5103038665228185221" style="display:none">This is a book I will like more in the future as I think back on it than I do right now having just finished it. The storyline was fine, but the execution of it fell flat for me. I was never completely drawn into the story until about the last hundred pages. Most of this was due to the splitting of the storyline with Kendra on a mission at Lost Mesa in Arizona while Seth stayed at Fablehaven and had adventures there. It felt very choppy as we jumped back and forth between the two storylines. Maybe Mull should have gone with Kendra until she left Lost Mesa, then jumped back and filled us in on the events happening at the same time at Fablehaven. In fact, if I ever read this one again, that's how I'm going to read it. I think the story will flow much better that way. <br /><br />There were some things I really liked about this book, though. The last 100 pages were very exciting! Also, Seth is starting to grow up and this time I was only really mad at him a couple of times. And, even though it was a very small part of the adventures at Lost Mesa, I loved the jackalopes! I don't recall ever reading any other book with jackalopes. Just fun! I’m already starting to like this book more now than I did while I was reading it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5103038665228185221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9725381204536414098" style="display:none">Wow! This series is on a roll. I was on the waiting list for about 4 months for this one. This is one of my favorite 3 or 4 young adult series. It's right up there with Harry Potter, The Bartimaeus Trilogy, and...not much else up this high. Maybe Gregor the Overlander...<br /><br />The characters are believable, there's always action but it is fresh each time, the plot twists and suspense are awesome, it's incredibly creative--I just love this series! The story slowly expands each book in a neat way. It started out as kids and family adventure in a small geographic location, but the action is intruding on their normal lives more and more and going more places. Highly recommended! </span>

<div id="review_2843443910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2843443910" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2843443910?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenny" href="/user/show/52409251-kenny">Kenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788377476727" href="/book/show/17902684-ba-niob-r-plaga-cieni">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52409251-kenny?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52409251-kenny?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52409251-kenny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2843443910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14182122521534983130">Every next book<br/><br/>  of this series the books are geting more and more  facinating.           <br/><br/>Brandon Mull is a great writer. He's one of my favourite writers, and Fablehaven is so interesting that you know that you want to read whole series even if you are still not finished with  current book.<br/><br/>The adventures of main characters are amazing. New magic creatures, objects, demons and reserves are awesome too. And the Brandon Dorman's illustrations are super!<br/><br/>When you are reading this book, it feels like</span>
  <span id="freeText14182122521534983130" style="display:none">Every next book<br /><br />  of this series the books are geting more and more  facinating.           <br /><br />Brandon Mull is a great writer. He's one of my favourite writers, and Fablehaven is so interesting that you know that you want to read whole series even if you are still not finished with  current book.<br /><br />The adventures of main characters are amazing. New magic creatures, objects, demons and reserves are awesome too. And the Brandon Dorman's illustrations are super!<br /><br />When you are reading this book, it feels like you are being a part of it.<br /><br />You see this world through the eyes of imagination.<br /><br />Thank you, Brandon Mull, for  writing  the Grip of the Shadow Plague and I can't wait to get to the next book of this series.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2684339840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2684339840" />
    <a title="AndaL_E2  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85625936-andal-e2"><img alt="AndaL_E2  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540382109p2/85625936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2684339840?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AndaL_E2  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="AndaL_E2  " href="/user/show/85625936-andal-e2">AndaL_E2  </a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2684339840&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2684339840" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4212972309953020043">Brandon Mull's creativity continued to shine throughout this book. The ideas of different disasters and magical objects were mindblowing. In this book, Kendra encounters a magnificent pyramid in a sanctuary and dangers lurking inside of it. While Seth encounters a weird disease that turns creatures dark and humans into shadow form. Then a plot twist came and made Kendra retreat back to fablehaven. While on the other hand, Seth found the artifact that controls time which brought the famous advent</span>
  <span id="freeText4212972309953020043" style="display:none">Brandon Mull's creativity continued to shine throughout this book. The ideas of different disasters and magical objects were mindblowing. In this book, Kendra encounters a magnificent pyramid in a sanctuary and dangers lurking inside of it. While Seth encounters a weird disease that turns creatures dark and humans into shadow form. Then a plot twist came and made Kendra retreat back to fablehaven. While on the other hand, Seth found the artifact that controls time which brought the famous adventurer Patton Burgess to him. The main theme in this story was 'love'. Not only the romantic kind but friendly love and the family kind of love too. Lena jumped out of the pool and sacrificed herself for Patton since she loved him so much. Lena also didn't want Kendra to die since she is her good friend. Everyone, including Grandpa and Grandma Sorenson, wanted to sacrifice themselves instead of others. This is because of the love between them. The love is strong enough to make people unafraid of death.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4212972309953020043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6aFmamtl4+ZXjw8/c4pJYyK3GQG6zLQve25pwR5/O4lagvf1OrOC44OHoDZxENpXzi6u0F+zsM1cuZ7ky9PECg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Cpx8tOmrbTsoCHQWLVYoiXOEW1rr2v/HEumv04WZmZO5v+0ruH0MPvwA2x8vzLu9nx3siw6l+yU1Plj2UDVmEA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Niezwykle precyzyjnie jest w niej budowane napięcie – prosta na początku fabuła obfituje w nieoczekiwane zwroty, nic też nie zapowiada zaskakującego finału… Równie ważne jak pochłaniająca czytelnika akcja jest jednak to, że książka tak wyraziście mówi o emocjach współczesnych nastolatków – ich samotności, marzeniach, wyborach – oraz nieumiejętności budowania relacji zarówno z rówieśnikami, jak i z najbliższą rodziną.
